pythondef load_audio_from_bytes(audio_bytes: bytes) -> np.ndarray:
    log.info(f"Received audio: {len(audio_bytes)} bytes, first 8 bytes: {audio_bytes[:8].hex()}")

    # Browser-recorded webm/opus needs ffmpeg-based decoding
    from pydub import AudioSegment
    AudioSegment.converter = imageio_ffmpeg.get_ffmpeg_exe()

    try:
        # Detect format from magic bytes
        if audio_bytes[:4] == b'\x1a\x45\xdf\xa3':
            fmt = 'webm'
        elif audio_bytes[:4] == b'RIFF':
            fmt = 'wav'
        elif audio_bytes[:3] == b'ID3' or audio_bytes[:2] == b'\xff\xfb':
            fmt = 'mp3'
        elif audio_bytes[:4] == b'OggS':
            fmt = 'ogg'
        else:
            fmt = None

        log.info(f"Detected format: {fmt}")

        audio = AudioSegment.from_file(io.BytesIO(audio_bytes), format=fmt)
        audio = audio.set_channels(1).set_frame_rate(SR)
        samples = np.array(audio.get_array_of_samples(), dtype=np.float32)
        samples = samples / (2 ** 15)  # normalise int16 to float [-1, 1]

        log.info(f"Decoded audio: {len(samples)} samples at {SR}Hz")
        return samples

    except Exception as e:
        log.error(f"Audio decode failed: {type(e).__name__}: {e}")
        raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail=f"Cannot decode audio: {e}")

Replace your load_audio_from_bytes function with this version that uses ffmpeg directly via subprocess (more reliable than pydub on Windows):
pythondef load_audio_from_bytes(audio_bytes: bytes) -> np.ndarray:
    import subprocess
    log.info(f"Received audio: {len(audio_bytes)} bytes, first 8 bytes: {audio_bytes[:8].hex()}")

    ffmpeg_path = imageio_ffmpeg.get_ffmpeg_exe()
    log.info(f"Using ffmpeg at: {ffmpeg_path}")

    try:
        # Pipe webm bytes into ffmpeg, get raw float32 PCM out
        process = subprocess.run(
            [
                ffmpeg_path,
                "-loglevel", "error",
                "-i", "pipe:0",            # read from stdin
                "-f", "f32le",             # output: 32-bit float little-endian
                "-acodec", "pcm_f32le",
                "-ac", "1",                # mono
                "-ar", str(SR),            # target sample rate
                "pipe:1",                  # write to stdout
            ],
            input=audio_bytes,
            capture_output=True,
            timeout=10,
        )

        if process.returncode != 0:
            err = process.stderr.decode(errors="ignore")
            log.error(f"ffmpeg failed: {err}")
            raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail=f"ffmpeg decode error: {err[:200]}")

        samples = np.frombuffer(process.stdout, dtype=np.float32)
        log.info(f"Decoded audio: {len(samples)} samples at {SR}Hz")

        if len(samples) == 0:
            raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail="ffmpeg produced no audio")

        return samples

    except subprocess.TimeoutExpired:
        log.error("ffmpeg timed out")
        raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail="Audio decoding timed out")
    except HTTPException:
        raise
    except Exception as e:
        log.error(f"Audio decode failed: {type(e).__name__}: {e}")
        raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail=f"Cannot decode audio: {e}")
You can also remove from pydub import AudioSegment and AudioSegment.converter = ... lines since we're not using pydub anymore вАФ but it's fine to leave them, they won't cause errors.

Counting:

Basic (what main.py does now): MFCC(40) + ќФ(40) + ќФќФ(40) = 120 channels
Richer (what your model expects): MFCC(40) + ќФ(40) + ќФќФ(40) + Mel(64) + Chroma(12) + Contrast(7) = 203 channels

Fix вАФ replace your extract_features function in main.py with this:
pythondef extract_features(y: np.ndarray) -> np.ndarray:
    """Rich feature stack matching the trained model:
       MFCC(40) + ќФ(40) + ќФќФ(40) + Mel(64) + Chroma(12) + Contrast(7) = 203
    """
    # Timbral features
    mfcc   = librosa.feature.mfcc(y=y, sr=SR, n_mfcc=N_MFCC,
                                   n_fft=N_FFT, hop_length=HOP_LENGTH)
    delta  = librosa.feature.delta(mfcc)
    delta2 = librosa.feature.delta(mfcc, order=2)

    # Spectral envelope
    mel    = librosa.feature.melspectrogram(y=y, sr=SR, n_mels=64,
                                             n_fft=N_FFT, hop_length=HOP_LENGTH)
    mel_db = librosa.power_to_db(mel, ref=np.max)

    # Pitch class
    chroma = librosa.feature.chroma_stft(y=y, sr=SR,
                                          n_fft=N_FFT, hop_length=HOP_LENGTH)

    # Spectral peaks/valleys
    contrast = librosa.feature.spectral_contrast(y=y, sr=SR,
                                                  n_fft=N_FFT, hop_length=HOP_LENGTH)

    features = np.vstack([mfcc, delta, delta2, mel_db, chroma, contrast])
    return features.astype(np.float32)

It's structured as both theory and hands-on practice.
The Big Idea
Instead of training a CNN from scratch (which needs lots of data and time), reuse a model that's already been trained on millions of ImageNet images. The pretrained model has already learned generic image features like edges, textures, and shapes, so you only need to teach it the specific classes for your new task.
How the Notebook Is Organised
Part 1 вАФ Theory (Cells 0вАУ8) explains what transfer learning is, why it works, and how it compares to training a CNN from scratch. The key insight is that early CNN layers learn generic features (edges, lines), middle layers learn textures and shapes, and only the deepest layers learn task-specific features. Since the early and middle layers are useful for most image tasks, you can reuse them and only retrain the final classifier.
It introduces two strategies:

Feature extraction вАФ freeze all pretrained layers, only train a new classifier on top. Good for small datasets.
Fine-tuning вАФ unfreeze some deeper layers and train them along with the classifier at a smaller learning rate. Good when you have more data.

Part 2 вАФ Practical setup (Cells 9вАУ33) does the standard PyTorch boilerplate: imports, device setup (CPU/GPU), mounting Google Drive, pointing to the Nigerian Food Dataset folder structure, creating ImageFolder datasets and DataLoader batches, and defining reusable helper functions for training (train_step, test_step, train, plot_loss_curves, accuracy_fn).
Part 3 вАФ Model 1: EfficientNet-B0 (Cells 34вАУ44) is the first practical example:

Load pretrained EfficientNet-B0 weights and the recommended image transforms (weights.transforms() automatically handles resize, crop, normalisation)
Freeze all feature extraction layers (param.requires_grad = False)
Replace the final classifier вАФ the original was trained for 1000 ImageNet classes, but the Nigerian Food Dataset has a different number, so a fresh Linear layer is dropped in
Train for 5 epochs with Adam optimiser at learning rate 0.001
Plot the loss and accuracy curves

Part 4 вАФ Model 2: ResNet18 (Cells 45вАУ59) repeats the same flow with a different architecture. ResNet introduced skip connections that let information flow more easily through deep networks. The replacement layer this time is .fc (instead of .classifier) because each architecture names its final layer differently.
Part 5 вАФ Comparison and inference (Cells 60вАУ65) compares the two models side by side with a bar chart of test accuracy, then shows how to use the trained model to classify a single new image.
Part 6 вАФ Fine-tuning extension (Cells 66вАУ68) demonstrates the second strategy: unfreezing the last block of EfficientNet-B0 and training it with a smaller learning rate (0.0001 instead of 0.001). The smaller learning rate is important вАФ too high and you destroy the useful pretrained weights.
Part 7 вАФ Saving the model (Cells 69вАУ70) uses torch.save(model.state_dict(), path) to persist the trained weights.
Part 8 вАФ Summary, exercises, and exam questions (Cells 71вАУ73) wraps up with the key teaching point ("don't train from scratch when you can reuse pretrained features"), three exercises for students (try other architectures, fine-tune more layers, write a comparison report), and exam-style questions covering the theoretical concepts.
How This Relates to Your CrySense Project
The pattern in this notebook is essentially what we did with your CrySense model вАФ load a pretrained EfficientNet-B0, freeze the base, replace the final classifier with one that matches your 4 cry classes, train the head, then optionally unfreeze and fine-tune. The main difference is your CrySense model uses 1D convolutions over MFCC features (audio domain) while this notebook uses 2D convolutions over images.оБЦоАїоГїоГєоГОYou said: write my chapter 4 and 5 for me based on the template as I have finished building my project, cry sense .Template for Chapter 4 and 5.docxdocxCrySense_Chapter4.docxdocxwrite my chapter 4 and 5 for me based on the template as I have finished building my project, cry sense . leave space for me to add screenshots21 MayоГОоБ§оБЦоАїClaude responded: Now I have the full template.Ran 2 commands, viewed a fileRan 2 commands, viewed a fileNow I have the full template. 4.4 CNN Model Architecture
The CrySense classification model is a one-dimensional Convolutional Neural Network (1D CNN) augmented with a Bidirectional Gated Recurrent Unit (BiGRU) and an attention pooling mechanism. The architecture was designed to process the 203-channel audio feature representation extracted from each three-second cry recording, where the input to the network has the shape (130, 203), corresponding to 130 time frames and 203 feature channels per frame.
The design philosophy behind this architecture combines three complementary modelling strategies. The convolutional layers act as local feature extractors that learn short-time acoustic patterns within the cry signal. The bidirectional recurrent layer models the temporal evolution of the cry across the full duration of the clip in both forward and backward directions. Finally, the attention pooling layer enables the network to assign greater importance to the most informative moments of the cry, rather than treating every time frame as equally relevant. Together, these components allow the model to capture both the fine-grained spectral characteristics and the longer-range temporal dynamics that distinguish one cry type from another.
4.4.1 Layer Architecture
The model is organised into four functional stages: a convolutional feature extraction stage, a recurrent sequence modelling stage, an attention pooling stage, and a dense classification head. The complete layer-by-layer structure is presented in the table below.
Layer (Type)Output ShapeParametersDescriptionInput(130, 203)0203-channel feature stack, 130 time framesConv1D (Block 1)(130, 96)136,51296 filters, kernel size 7, ReLU, L2 regularisedBatchNormalization(130, 96)384Stabilises activationsConv1D (Block 1)(130, 96)46,17696 filters, kernel size 5, ReLUBatchNormalization(130, 96)384Stabilises activationsMaxPooling1D(65, 96)0Pool size 2, halves time dimensionDropout(65, 96)0Rate 0.25Conv1D (Block 2)(65, 192)92,352192 filters, kernel size 5, ReLUBatchNormalization(65, 192)768Stabilises activationsConv1D (Block 2)(65, 192)110,784192 filters, kernel size 3, ReLUBatchNormalization(65, 192)768Stabilises activationsMaxPooling1D(32, 192)0Pool size 2Dropout(32, 192)0Rate 0.30Conv1D (Block 3)(32, 384)221,568384 filters, kernel size 3, ReLUBatchNormalization(32, 384)1,536Stabilises activationsMaxPooling1D(16, 384)0Pool size 2Dropout(16, 384)0Rate 0.35Bidirectional GRU(16, 256)394,752128 units per directionDense (Attention)(16, 1)257Attention scoring, tanh activationFlatten(16)0Flattens attention scoresActivation (Softmax)(16)0Normalises attention weightsRepeatVector(256, 16)0Broadcasts attention across featuresPermute(16, 256)0Reorders dimensionsMultiply(16, 256)0Applies attention to GRU outputGlobalAveragePooling1D(256)0Aggregates weighted featuresDense(128)32,896128 units, ReLU, L2 regularisedBatchNormalization(128)512Stabilises activationsDropout(128)0Rate 0.40Dense (Output)(4)516Softmax, 4 classes
The model contains approximately 1,040,165 total parameters, of which 1,037,989 are trainable and 2,176 are non-trainable (the non-trainable parameters belong to the batch normalisation layers). The total model size is approximately 3.97 MB, which is compact enough to be deployed on resource-constrained environments and converted to the ONNX format for efficient inference.
The three convolutional blocks progressively increase the number of filters (96, 192, 384) while reducing the temporal resolution through max pooling. This is a standard hierarchical design in which early layers capture low-level acoustic features such as energy bursts and pitch transitions, while deeper layers capture higher-level abstractions that combine these primitives. Dropout is applied after each block at increasing rates (0.25, 0.30, 0.35) to progressively regularise the deeper, more expressive layers and reduce overfitting. The Bidirectional GRU then processes the resulting feature sequence, and the attention mechanism produces a single weighted summary vector that is passed to the dense classifier.
4.4.2 Model Compilation
After the architecture was defined, the model was compiled with the components required for training. The compilation configuration is summarised below.
ComponentConfigurationJustificationOptimiserAdamAdaptive learning rate optimiser that combines momentum and per-parameter scaling, suitable for noisy gradientsLearning RateCosine decay with restarts, initial 1e-3Allows rapid early learning and fine refinement in later epochsLoss FunctionSparse Categorical Cross-EntropyAppropriate for multi-class classification with integer-encoded labelsEvaluation MetricAccuracyPrimary metric for monitoring training and validation performanceOutput ActivationSoftmaxProduces a probability distribution across the four cry classes
The Adam optimiser was selected over alternatives such as stochastic gradient descent because it adapts the learning rate for each parameter individually, which accelerates convergence on the heterogeneous audio feature space. The sparse categorical cross-entropy loss was used because the class labels are stored as integers (0 for hunger, 1 for pain, 2 for discomfort, 3 for sleepiness) rather than one-hot encoded vectors, making it the memory-efficient choice. The softmax activation in the output layer ensures that the four output values sum to one and can be interpreted as the model's confidence in each class.
4.4.3 Training Configuration
The model was trained using a configuration designed to maximise generalisation on a moderately sized, augmented dataset. The full training configuration is presented below.
ParameterValuePurposeMaximum Epochs80Upper bound on training iterationsBatch Size64Number of samples processed per gradient updateLearning Rate ScheduleCosine Decay with Restarts (initial 1e-3)Cyclical learning rate for better convergenceClass WeightsBalanced (computed from training distribution)Counteracts residual class imbalanceEarly StoppingMonitor validation accuracy, patience 15Halts training when validation accuracy stops improvingModel CheckpointSave best by validation accuracyRetains the best-performing weightsValidation Split15% of total datasetHeld-out set for monitoring during training
Several techniques were employed to ensure robust training and prevent overfitting. Class weights were computed from the training distribution and passed to the training process, so that the under-represented classes (pain, discomfort, and sleepiness) contributed proportionally more to the loss than their raw sample counts would otherwise allow. This counteracts the model's natural tendency to favour the dominant hunger class.
Early stopping was configured to monitor validation accuracy with a patience of 15 epochs, meaning training would automatically halt if the validation accuracy failed to improve for 15 consecutive epochs. Combined with model checkpointing, which saved the model weights only when a new best validation accuracy was achieved, this ensured that the final model corresponded to the epoch of peak generalisation performance rather than the final epoch of training. The cosine decay learning rate schedule with warm restarts allowed the optimiser to periodically increase the learning rate to escape shallow local minima, then decay it again for fine-grained convergence, which contributed to the model's final stability.

The parameter counts and output shapes in the layer architecture table come directly from your model summary that you shared earlier, so they're accurate to your actual model. If you re-train and the numbers shift slightly, just update the affected cells. Cell A вАФ Per-Class Performance Curves (Precision-Recall + ROC)
python# вФАвФА BLOCK 8b: PER-CLASS PERFORMANCE CURVES вФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФА
# Precision-Recall and ROC curves for each of the 4 classes
# Uses one-vs-rest since this is a multi-class problem

import numpy as np
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
from sklearn.metrics import precision_recall_curve, roc_curve, auc
from sklearn.preprocessing import label_binarize

# Use the best saved model
best_model = tf.keras.models.load_model(f'{MODEL_DIR}/crysense_best.h5')

# Get prediction probabilities for the whole test set

# Binarise the true labels for one-vs-rest curves
y_test_bin = label_binarize(y_test, classes=[0, 1, 2, 3])  # shape (n, 4)

class_colours = ['#F59E0B', '#EF4444', '#8B5CF6', '#3B82F6']

# вФАвФА Precision-Recall curve per class вФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФА

    roc_auc = auc(fpr, tpr)
    plt.plot(fpr, tpr, color=class_colours[i], linewidth=2,
             label=f'{cls} (AUC = {roc_auc:.3f})')

Cell B вАФ Precision and Recall Per Class (bar chart + table)
python# вФАвФА BLOCK 8c: PRECISION & RECALL PER CLASS вФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФА

Cell C вАФ 5-Fold Cross-Validation
python# вФАвФА BLOCK 8d: 5-FOLD STRATIFIED CROSS-VALIDATION вФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФА
# Re-trains the model on 5 different train/test splits to confirm
# the result is stable and not dependent on one lucky split.
# NOTE: this re-uses the full feature set X, y (before the single split)

from sklearn.model_selection import StratifiedKFold

N_FOLDS = 5
skf = StratifiedKFold(n_splits=N_FOLDS, shuffle=True, random_state=42)

fold_accuracies = []
fold_num = 1

# X is (samples, channels, time) вАФ transpose to (samples, time, channels) for Conv1D
X_cv = X.transpose(0, 2, 1)

print(f"Running {N_FOLDS}-fold cross-validation...\n")

for train_idx, test_idx in skf.split(X_cv, y):
    print(f"вФАвФАвФАвФАвФА Fold {fold_num}/{N_FOLDS} вФАвФАвФАвФАвФА")

    X_tr, X_te = X_cv[train_idx], X_cv[test_idx]
    y_tr, y_te = y[train_idx], y[test_idx]

    # Normalise using THIS fold's training stats only (no leakage)
    fold_mean = X_tr.mean()
    fold_std  = X_tr.std()
    X_tr = (X_tr - fold_mean) / fold_std
    X_te = (X_te - fold_mean) / fold_std

    # Class weights for this fold
    cw_arr = compute_class_weight('balanced', classes=np.unique(y_tr), y=y_tr)
    cw = dict(enumerate(cw_arr))

    # Fresh model each fold
    fold_model = build_cry_classifier(X_tr.shape[1:])

    # Train (fewer epochs than full run, with early stopping, to keep CV fast)
    fold_model.fit(
        X_tr, y_tr,
        validation_data=(X_te, y_te),
        epochs=40,
        batch_size=64,
        class_weight=cw,
        callbacks=[
            tf.keras.callbacks.EarlyStopping(
                monitor='val_accuracy', patience=8,
                restore_best_weights=True, verbose=0
            )
        ],
        verbose=0
    )

    # Evaluate this fold
    _, fold_acc = fold_model.evaluate(X_te, y_te, verbose=0)
    fold_accuracies.append(fold_acc)
    print(f"  Fold {fold_num} accuracy: {fold_acc:.4f}\n")
    fold_num += 1

    # Free memory
    del fold_model
    tf.keras.backend.clear_session()

# вФАвФА Summary вФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФА
fold_accuracies = np.array(fold_accuracies)
mean_acc = fold_accuracies.mean()
std_acc  = fold_accuracies.std()

print("=" * 40)
print("Cross-Validation Results")
print("=" * 40)
for i, acc in enumerate(fold_accuracies, 1):
    print(f"  Fold {i}: {acc:.4f}")
print("-" * 40)
print(f"  Mean accuracy:      {mean_acc:.4f}")
print(f"  Standard deviation: {std_acc:.4f}")

# вФАвФА Bar chart of fold accuracies вФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФАвФА
plt.figure(figsize=(9, 5))
bars = plt.bar(range(1, N_FOLDS + 1), fold_accuracies, color='#4C72B0', alpha=0.85)
plt.axhline(mean_acc, color='#DD8452', linestyle='--', linewidth=2,
            label=f'Mean = {mean_acc:.3f}')
plt.xlabel('Fold', fontsize=12)
plt.ylabel('Accuracy', fontsize=12)
plt.title(f'{N_FOLDS}-Fold Cross-Validation Accuracy', fontsize=13, fontweight='bold')
plt.xticks(range(1, N_FOLDS + 1))
plt.ylim(0, 1.0)
plt.legend()
plt.grid(axis='y', alpha=0.3)

for bar, acc in zip(bars, fold_accuracies):
    plt.annotate(f'{acc:.3f}', xy=(bar.get_x() + bar.get_width()/2, acc),
                 xytext=(0, 3), textcoords='offset points',
                 ha='center', fontsize=9)

plt.tight_layout()
plt.savefig(f'{MODEL_DIR}/cross_validation.png', dpi=150)
plt.show()

How to use them
Add these three cells after Block 8 (your existing evaluation cell, cell index 10). They depend on variables that already exist by that point: X_test_t, y_test, CLASSES, MODEL_DIR, build_cry_classifier, compute_class_weight, and the raw X, y.
Run order:

Cell A вАФ saves precision_recall_curves.png and roc_curves.png
Cell B вАФ saves precision_recall_per_class.png and prints the table you can paste into section 4.4
Cell C вАФ saves cross_validation.png and prints the fold table for section 4.4.1.4

One note on Cell C: cross-validation re-trains the model five times, so it will take a while (roughly 5√Ч the time of one training run, though shortened here to 40 epochs per fold with early stopping). If you're short on time before a deadline, you can lower epochs=40 to epochs=25 вАФ the fold accuracies will be slightly lower but the stability picture (low standard deviation) will still come through.

How push works end to end
When a cry is detected, the flow is: FastAPI returns the prediction вЖТ NestJS saves it to history, creates an alert, and (if push is enabled) calls PushService.sendToAll() вЖТ the browser's service worker (sw.js) receives the push event and shows a system notification, even if the CrySense tab is closed.
The user enables it by toggling "Push notifications" in Settings, which triggers the browser permission prompt and registers the subscription with your backend.
Important note for testing
Web Push requires HTTPS in production, but works on http://localhost for development. When you deploy, you'll need an HTTPS domain for push to function. For your final year project demo on localhost, it works as-is.
You'll also want two small icon files in public/ вАФ icon-192.png (192√Ч192) for the notification icon. Any placeholder PNG works for the demo.

Let me give you a workaround that generates the keys directly.
Option 1: Generate keys with a small script
Create a temporary file genkeys.js in your backend/ folder:
javascriptconst webpush = require('web-push');
const keys = webpush.generateVAPIDKeys();
console.log('VAPID_PUBLIC_KEY=' + keys.publicKey);
console.log('VAPID_PRIVATE_KEY=' + keys.privateKey);
Then run it:
powershellcd C:\Users\somto\Desktop\finalyear\crysensecode\backend
node genkeys.js
It will print:
VAPID_PUBLIC_KEY=BNc...
VAPID_PRIVATE_KEY=xVz...
Copy those two lines into your backend/.env file. Then delete genkeys.js since you only need to run it once.
Option 2: Reinstall web-push first
If node genkeys.js also fails with "Cannot find module 'web-push'", the package didn't install properly. Reinstall it:
powershellcd C:\Users\somto\Desktop\finalyear\crysensecode\backend
npm install web-push
Then run node genkeys.js again.

The reason npx web-push generate-vapid-keys failed is that newer versions of the web-push npm package changed where they put the CLI file, and npx couldn't find it. Generating the keys programmatically with the small script avoids the CLI entirely and always works.
Once you have the keys in .env, continue with the rest of the setup.оБЦоАїоГїоГєоГОYou said: history.history.service keeps showing these errors26 MayоГОоБ§оБЦоАїClaude responded: Those red squiggles are just ESLint warnings, not actual errors.Those red squiggles are just ESLint warnings, not actual errors. "Unsafe assignment of an any value" is the strict TypeScript ESLint rule complaining that result is typed as any. Your code will compile and run perfectly fine вАФ these are style warnings, not blockers.
You have two options:
Option 1: Ignore them (they don't break anything)
Run the backend anyway:
powershellcd C:\Users\somto\Desktop\finalyear\crysensecode\backend
npm run start:dev
If it starts and works, the warnings are cosmetic. You can leave them.
Option 2: Make them go away by typing result properly
The warnings appear because save(result: any) uses any. Give it a proper type. Open history.service.ts and change the save method signature.
Find this:
typescriptasync save(result: any): Promise<void> {
Replace with:
typescriptasync save(result: {
  id: string;
  babyId?: string;
  primaryCause: string;
  primaryConfidence: number;
  contextAdjustedCause: string;
  fusionApplied: boolean;
  fusionReason?: string;
  recommendation: string;
  actionItems: string[];
  allProbabilities: Record<string, number>;
  modelLatencyMs: number;
  totalLatencyMs: number;
}): Promise<void> {
That tells TypeScript exactly what result contains, so the "unsafe any" warnings disappear.
Option 3: Turn off the strict rule entirely
If you'd rather not bother with typing and just want the warnings gone everywhere, open eslint.config.mjs in your backend root and add these rules:
javascriptrules: {
  '@typescript-eslint/no-unsafe-assignment': 'off',
  '@typescript-eslint/no-unsafe-member-access': 'off',
  '@typescript-eslint/no-explicit-any': 'off',
},

My recommendation: try Option 1 first. Run npm run start:dev and see if the backend boots. These ESLint warnings almost never stop a NestJS app from running вАФ they're just the linter being strict. If it runs, you can either leave the warnings or apply Option 2 to clean them up for your final submission.
What does the terminal show when you run npm run start:dev?оБЦоАїоГїоГєоГОYou said: use option 2 for the entire file:use option 2 for the entire file: import { Injectable } from '@nestjs/common';
import { InjectRepository } from '@nestjs/typeorm';
import { Repository } from 'typeorm';
import { DetectionEntity } from '../entities/detection.entity';
@Injectable()
export class HistoryService {
  constructor(
    @InjectRepository(DetectionEntity)
    private readonly repo: Repository<DetectionEntity>,
  ) {}
  /** Persist a detection result (called by the detection flow). */
  
  async save(result: any): Promise<void> {
    const entity = this.repo.create({
      id: result.id,
      babyId: result.b
abyId ?? null,
      primaryCause: result.primaryCause,
      primaryConfidence: result.primaryConfidence,
      contextAdjustedCause: result.contextAdjustedCause,
      fusionApplied: result.fusionApplied,
      fusionReason: result.fusionReason ?? null,
      recommendation: result.recommendation,
      actionItems: JSON.stringify(result.actionItems),
      allProbabilities: JSON.stringify(result.allProbabilities),
      modelLatencyMs: result.modelLatencyMs,
      totalLatencyMs: result.totalLatencyMs,
    });
    await this.repo.save(entity);
  }
  /** Return detection history, newest first. */
  async findAll(limit = 100): Promise<any[]> {
    const rows = await this.repo.find({
      order: { createdAt: 'DESC' },
      take: limit,
    });
    // Deserialise JSON columns back into objects
    return rows.map((r) => ({
      id: r.id,
      primaryCause: r.primaryCause,
      primaryConfidence: r.primaryConfidence,
      contextAdjustedCause: r.contextAdjustedCause,
      fusionApplied: r.fusionApplied,
      fusionReason: r.fusionReason,
      recommendation: r.recommendation,
      actionItems: JSON.parse(r.actionItems),
      allProbabilities: JSON.parse(r.allProbabilities),
      modelLatencyMs: r.modelLatencyMs,

    }));

Here's the complete clean file with proper typing. Select all in history.service.ts (Ctrl+A), delete, and paste this:
typescriptimport { Injectable } from '@nestjs/common';
import { InjectRepository } from '@nestjs/typeorm';
import { Repository } from 'typeorm';
import { DetectionEntity } from '../entities/detection.entity';

// Shape of a detection result coming in to be saved
export interface DetectionInput {
  id: string;
  babyId?: string;
  primaryCause: string;
  primaryConfidence: number;
  contextAdjustedCause: string;
  fusionApplied: boolean;
  fusionReason?: string;
  recommendation: string;
  actionItems: string[];
  allProbabilities: Record<string, number>;
  modelLatencyMs: number;
  totalLatencyMs: number;
}

// Shape of a detection result returned from history
export interface DetectionOutput {
  id: string;
  primaryCause: string;
  primaryConfidence: number;
  contextAdjustedCause: string;
  fusionApplied: boolean;
  fusionReason: string | null;
  recommendation: string;
  actionItems: string[];
  allProbabilities: Record<string, number>;
  modelLatencyMs: number;
  totalLatencyMs: number;
  timestamp: string;
}

@Injectable()
export class HistoryService {
  constructor(
    @InjectRepository(DetectionEntity)
    private readonly repo: Repository<DetectionEntity>,
  ) {}

  /** Persist a detection result (called by the detection flow). */
  async save(result: DetectionInput): Promise<void> {
    const entity = this.repo.create({
      id: result.id,
      babyId: result.babyId ?? null,
      primaryCause: result.primaryCause,
      primaryConfidence: result.primaryConfidence,
      contextAdjustedCause: result.contextAdjustedCause,
      fusionApplied: result.fusionApplied,
      fusionReason: result.fusionReason ?? null,
      recommendation: result.recommendation,
      actionItems: JSON.stringify(result.actionItems),
      allProbabilities: JSON.stringify(result.allProbabilities),
      modelLatencyMs: result.modelLatencyMs,
      totalLatencyMs: result.totalLatencyMs,
    });
    await this.repo.save(entity);
  }

  /** Return detection history, newest first. */
  async findAll(limit = 100): Promise<DetectionOutput[]> {
    const rows = await this.repo.find({
      order: { createdAt: 'DESC' },
      take: limit,
    });
    // Deserialise JSON columns back into objects
    return rows.map((r) => ({
      id: r.id,
      primaryCause: r.primaryCause,
      primaryConfidence: r.primaryConfidence,
      contextAdjustedCause: r.contextAdjustedCause,
      fusionApplied: r.fusionApplied,
      fusionReason: r.fusionReason,
      recommendation: r.recommendation,
      actionItems: JSON.parse(r.actionItems) as string[],
      allProbabilities: JSON.parse(r.allProbabilities) as Record<string, number>,
      modelLatencyMs: r.modelLatencyMs,
      totalLatencyMs: r.totalLatencyMs,
      timestamp: r.createdAt.toISOString(),
    }));
  }

  async clear(): Promise<void> {
    await this.repo.clear();
  }
}
Key changes that remove all the warnings:

Added DetectionInput interface вАФ types the save() parameter so result.xxx accesses are no longer "unsafe any"
Added DetectionOutput interface вАФ types the return value of findAll()
Added as string[] and as Record<string, number> on the JSON.parse() calls вАФ JSON.parse returns any, so casting it tells ESLint what type to expect
Fixed the result.babyId typo that was split across two lines in your version

Found 6 error(s).Show more27 MayоГОоБ§оБЦоАїClaude responded: TypeScript strict mode is flagging that some entity columns could be undefined.TypeScript strict mode is flagging that some entity columns could be undefined. Two files to fix.
Fix 1: src/entities/settings.entity.ts
The columns with defaults are typed as optionally undefined. Make them definite. Open the file and add ! after each column name:
typescriptimport { Entity, PrimaryColumn, Column } from 'typeorm';

@Entity('settings')
export class SettingsEntity {
  @PrimaryColumn()
  id!: string;

  @Column({ default: true })
  pushNotifications!: boolean;

  @Column({ default: true })
  temperatureAlerts!: boolean;

  @Column('float', { default: 20 })
  tempMin!: number;

  @Column('float', { default: 26 })
  tempMax!: number;
}
The ! is the "definite assignment assertion" вАФ it tells TypeScript that TypeORM will always populate these fields even though the constructor doesn't.
Fix 2: src/entities/push-subscription.entity.ts
Same fix:
typescriptimport { Entity, PrimaryGeneratedColumn, Column, CreateDateColumn } from 'typeorm';

@Entity('push_subscriptions')
export class PushSubscriptionEntity {
  @PrimaryGeneratedColumn('uuid')
  id!: string;

  @Column('text', { unique: true })
  endpoint!: string;

  @Column('text')
  p256dh!: string;

  @Column('text')
  auth!: string;

  @CreateDateColumn()
  createdAt!: Date;
}
Apply the same fix to all entities
While you're at it, add ! to the column properties in your other two entity files too (detection.entity.ts and alert.entity.ts), or you'll get the same errors when those are checked. Every @Column, @PrimaryColumn, @PrimaryGeneratedColumn, and @CreateDateColumn property should have ! after its name.
For example in detection.entity.ts:
typescript@PrimaryColumn()
id!: string;

@Column({ nullable: true })
@Index()
babyId!: string;
And alert.entity.ts:
typescript@PrimaryGeneratedColumn('uuid')
id!: string;

@Column()
type!: 'cry' | 'temperature';
Then rebuild
powershellnpm run build
All 6 errors should clear. The root cause is that TypeScript's strict mode doesn't know TypeORM populates entity fields at runtime, so the ! assertion tells it "trust me, this will have a value." This is the standard, recommended way to write TypeORM entities in strict mode.оБЦоАїоГїоГєоГОYou said: [Nest] 27360  - 27/05/2026, 13:55:03   ERROR [ExceptionHandler] MissingDriverError: Wrong driver: "undefined" given.[Nest] 27360  - 27/05/2026, 13:55:03   ERROR [ExceptionHandler] MissingDriverError: Wrong driver: "undefined" given.     at <anonymous> (C:\Users\somto\Desktop\finalyear\crysensecode\bacpasted27 MayоГОоБ§оБЦоАїClaude responded: The error Data type "Object" in "DetectionEntity.The error Data type "Object" in "DetectionEntity.id" means TypeORM can't figure out the column type for id. Open backend/tsconfig.json and make sure these two lines are present and true under compilerOptions:
json{

    "emitDecoratorMetadata": true,

Fix 2: Type the result properly
The errors say 'result' is of type 'unknown'. That's because api.detect() returns Promise<any> but TypeScript's strict mode is treating it as unknown. Let me give you a clean, fully-typed DetectScreen.tsx. Select all in your existing file (Ctrl+A), delete, and paste this:
typescriptimport { useState, useRef, useEffect } from 'react';
import { Mic, MicOff, Loader2, CheckCircle, AlertCircle, Thermometer } from 'lucide-react';
import { theme } from '../lib/theme';
import { api } from '../lib/api';
import { CLASS_LABEL, CLASS_EMOJI, CLASS_COLOUR } from '../components/shared';
import { TopBar } from '../components/TopBar';

const RECORDING_DURATION_MS = 4000;
type Stage = 'idle' | 'requesting' | 'recording' | 'processing' | 'result' | 'error';

interface DetectionResult {
  id: string;
  primaryCause: string;
  primaryConfidence: number;
  contextAdjustedCause: string;
  fusionApplied: boolean;
  fusionReason?: string;
  recommendation: string;
  actionItems: string[];
  allProbabilities: Record<string, number>;
  modelLatencyMs: number;
  totalLatencyMs: number;
  timestamp: string;
}

export function DetectScreen({ onDetected }: { onDetected: () => void }) {
  const [stage, setStage] = useState<Stage>('idle');
  const [error, setError] = useState<string | null>(null);
  const [result, setResult] = useState<DetectionResult | null>(null);
  const [progress, setProgress] = useState(0);
  const [temp, setTemp] = useState<number | null>(null);

  const recorderRef = useRef<MediaRecorder | null>(null);
  const chunksRef = useRef<Blob[]>([]);
  const streamRef = useRef<MediaStream | null>(null);
  const timerRef = useRef<number | null>(null);
  const progRef = useRef<number | null>(null);

  useEffect(() => () => {
    if (timerRef.current) clearTimeout(timerRef.current);
    if (progRef.current) clearInterval(progRef.current);
    streamRef.current?.getTracks().forEach((t) => t.stop());
  }, []);

  const start = async () => {
    setError(null);
    setResult(null);
    setStage('requesting');
    try {
      const stream = await navigator.mediaDevices.getUserMedia({
        audio: { channelCount: 1, sampleRate: 22050 },
      });
      streamRef.current = stream;
      const mimeType = MediaRecorder.isTypeSupported('audio/webm;codecs=opus')
        ? 'audio/webm;codecs=opus'
        : 'audio/webm';
      const recorder = new MediaRecorder(stream, { mimeType });
      recorderRef.current = recorder;
      chunksRef.current = [];
      recorder.ondataavailable = (e) => {
        if (e.data.size > 0) chunksRef.current.push(e.data);
      };
      recorder.onstop = handleStop;
      recorder.start();
      setStage('recording');
      const startTime = Date.now();
      progRef.current = window.setInterval(() => {
        setProgress(Math.min(100, ((Date.now() - startTime) / RECORDING_DURATION_MS) * 100));
      }, 50);
      timerRef.current = window.setTimeout(stop, RECORDING_DURATION_MS);
    } catch (err) {
      setStage('error');
      const e = err as Error;
      setError(
        e.name === 'NotAllowedError'
          ? 'Microphone permission denied. Please enable it in your browser settings.'
          : 'Could not access microphone.',
      );
    }
  };

  const stop = () => {
    if (timerRef.current) clearTimeout(timerRef.current);
    if (progRef.current) clearInterval(progRef.current);
    if (recorderRef.current?.state === 'recording') recorderRef.current.stop();
    streamRef.current?.getTracks().forEach((t) => t.stop());
  };

  const handleStop = async () => {
    setStage('processing');
    const blob = new Blob(chunksRef.current, { type: 'audio/webm' });
    if (blob.size < 2000) {
      setStage('error');
      setError('Recording too short. Please try again.');
      return;
    }
    try {
      const fd = new FormData();
      fd.append('audio', blob, 'cry.webm');
      fd.append('timeOfDay', getTimeOfDay());
      const data = (await api.detect(fd)) as DetectionResult;
      setResult(data);
      onDetected();
      setStage('result');
    } catch (err) {
      setStage('error');
      setError((err as Error).message || 'Could not process the recording.');
    }
  };

  const reset = () => {
    setStage('idle');
    setResult(null);
    setError(null);
    setProgress(0);
  };

  const adjustTemp = async (delta: number) => {
    const newVal = parseFloat(((temp ?? 22) + delta).toFixed(1));
    setTemp(newVal);
    try {
      await api.reportTemperature(newVal);
      onDetected();
    } catch {
      // silent вАФ UI already updated
    }
  };

  return (
    <div style={{ paddingBottom: 90 }}>
      <TopBar title="CrySense" subtitle="Tap to detect what your baby needs" />

      <div style={{ padding: '28px 20px', display: 'flex', flexDirection: 'column', alignItems: 'center' }}>

        <div style={{
          width: '100%', maxWidth: 420, background: theme.colors.surface,
          border: `1px solid ${theme.colors.border}`, borderRadius: theme.radius.lg,
          padding: 16, marginBottom: 28, display: 'flex', alignItems: 'center', gap: 12,
        }}>
          <div style={{
            width: 40, height: 40, background: `${theme.colors.info}15`,
            color: theme.colors.info, borderRadius: 999,
            display: 'flex', alignItems: 'center', justifyContent: 'center',
          }}>
            <Thermometer size={18} />
          </div>
          <div style={{ flex: 1, minWidth: 0 }}>
            <div style={{
              fontSize: 11, color: theme.colors.textMuted, fontWeight: 600,
              letterSpacing: '0.05em', textTransform: 'uppercase',
            }}>
              Room Temperature
            </div>
            <div style={{ fontSize: 18, fontWeight: 700, color: theme.colors.text, marginTop: 1 }}>
              {temp !== null ? `${temp.toFixed(1)}¬∞C` : 'вАФ'}
            </div>
          </div>
          <div style={{ display: 'flex', gap: 4 }}>
            {[-0.5, 0.5].map((d) => (
              <button
                key={d}
                onClick={() => adjustTemp(d)}
                style={{
                  width: 32, height: 32, borderRadius: theme.radius.md,
                  background: theme.colors.surfaceAlt,
                  border: `1px solid ${theme.colors.border}`,
                  cursor: 'pointer', fontWeight: 700, color: theme.colors.text,
                }}
              >
                {d > 0 ? '+' : 'вИТ'}
              </button>
            ))}
          </div>
        </div>

        {stage === 'idle' && (
          <button onClick={start} style={tapStyle(theme.colors.primary)}>
            <Mic size={56} color="#fff" />
          </button>
        )}
        {stage === 'requesting' && (
          <div style={tapStyle(theme.colors.textMuted)}>
            <Loader2 size={48} color="#fff" className="spin" />
          </div>
        )}
        {stage === 'recording' && (
          <div style={{ position: 'relative' }}>
            <svg width={200} height={200} style={{ position: 'absolute', transform: 'rotate(-90deg)' }}>
              <circle cx={100} cy={100} r={92} fill="none"
                stroke={`${theme.colors.primary}20`} strokeWidth={5} />
              <circle cx={100} cy={100} r={92} fill="none"
                stroke={theme.colors.primary} strokeWidth={5} strokeLinecap="round"
                strokeDasharray={`${(progress / 100) * 578} 578`}
                style={{ transition: 'stroke-dasharray 0.05s linear' }} />
            </svg>
            <button onClick={stop} style={tapStyle(theme.colors.danger)}>
              <MicOff size={56} color="#fff" />
            </button>
          </div>
        )}
        {stage === 'processing' && (
          <div style={tapStyle(theme.colors.primary)}>
            <Loader2 size={48} color="#fff" className="spin" />
          </div>
        )}

        {(stage === 'idle' || stage === 'recording' || stage === 'processing') && (
          <p style={{ marginTop: 24, fontSize: 14, color: theme.colors.textMuted, textAlign: 'center' }}>
            {stage === 'idle' && 'Tap when baby is crying'}
            {stage === 'recording' && `ListeningвА¶ ${Math.round(progress)}%`}
            {stage === 'processing' && 'Analysing the cryвА¶'}
          </p>
        )}

        {stage === 'result' && result && <ResultCard result={result} onReset={reset} />}

        {stage === 'error' && (
          <div style={{
            width: '100%', maxWidth: 420, background: `${theme.colors.danger}08`,
            border: `1px solid ${theme.colors.danger}30`, borderRadius: theme.radius.lg,
            padding: 20, textAlign: 'center', marginTop: 24,
          }}>
            <AlertCircle size={28} color={theme.colors.danger} style={{ marginBottom: 8 }} />
            <p style={{ color: theme.colors.danger, marginBottom: 16, fontSize: 14 }}>{error}</p>
            <button onClick={reset} style={primaryBtn()}>Try again</button>
          </div>
        )}
      </div>
    </div>
  );
}

function ResultCard({ result, onReset }: { result: DetectionResult; onReset: () => void }) {
  const cause = result.contextAdjustedCause;
  const colour = CLASS_COLOUR[cause];
  const confPct = Math.round(result.primaryConfidence * 100);

  const sortedProbs: [string, number][] = Object.entries(result.allProbabilities)
    .sort((a, b) => b[1] - a[1]);

  return (
    <div style={{
      width: '100%', maxWidth: 420, marginTop: 24, background: theme.colors.surface,
      border: `1px solid ${theme.colors.border}`, borderRadius: theme.radius.lg, overflow: 'hidden',
    }}>
      <div style={{
        background: `${colour}10`, padding: '24px 24px 20px',
        textAlign: 'center', borderBottom: `1px solid ${theme.colors.borderLight}`,
      }}>
        <div style={{ fontSize: 48, marginBottom: 6 }}>{CLASS_EMOJI[cause]}</div>
        <div style={{ fontSize: 20, fontWeight: 700, color: colour }}>{CLASS_LABEL[cause]}</div>
        <div style={{ fontSize: 13, color: theme.colors.textMuted, marginTop: 2 }}>
          {confPct}% confidence
        </div>
      </div>

      <div style={{ padding: 20 }}>
        <p style={{ fontSize: 14, lineHeight: 1.5, color: theme.colors.text, marginTop: 0 }}>
          {result.recommendation}
        </p>

        <div style={{ marginTop: 16 }}>
          {result.actionItems.map((item: string, i: number) => (
            <div key={i} style={{
              display: 'flex', alignItems: 'flex-start', gap: 10, padding: '8px 0',
              borderTop: i === 0 ? 'none' : `1px solid ${theme.colors.borderLight}`,
            }}>
              <CheckCircle size={16} color={colour} style={{ marginTop: 2, flexShrink: 0 }} />
              <span style={{ fontSize: 13, lineHeight: 1.4, color: theme.colors.text }}>{item}</span>
            </div>
          ))}
        </div>

        <div style={{ marginTop: 20, paddingTop: 16, borderTop: `1px solid ${theme.colors.borderLight}` }}>
          {sortedProbs.map(([cls, prob]) => (
            <div key={cls} style={{ marginBottom: 8 }}>
              <div style={{ display: 'flex', justifyContent: 'space-between', fontSize: 12, marginBottom: 4 }}>
                <span style={{ color: theme.colors.text, fontWeight: 500 }}>{CLASS_LABEL[cls]}</span>
                <span style={{ color: theme.colors.textMuted }}>{Math.round(prob * 100)}%</span>
              </div>
              <div style={{ height: 4, background: theme.colors.surfaceAlt, borderRadius: 2 }}>
                <div style={{
                  height: '100%', width: `${prob * 100}%`,
                  background: CLASS_COLOUR[cls], borderRadius: 2, transition: 'width 0.4s',
                }} />
              </div>
            </div>
          ))}
        </div>

        {result.fusionApplied && result.fusionReason && (
          <div style={{
            marginTop: 16, padding: 12, background: `${theme.colors.warning}10`,
            border: `1px solid ${theme.colors.warning}30`, borderRadius: theme.radius.md,
            fontSize: 12, lineHeight: 1.5, color: theme.colors.text,
          }}>
            <strong style={{ color: theme.colors.warning }}>Context note: </strong>
            {result.fusionReason}
          </div>
        )}

        <button onClick={onReset} style={{ ...primaryBtn(), marginTop: 20 }}>
          <Mic size={16} /> Detect another cry
        </button>
      </div>
    </div>
  );
}

function tapStyle(colour: string): React.CSSProperties {
  return {
    width: 200, height: 200, borderRadius: '50%', background: colour, border: 'none',
    cursor: 'pointer', display: 'flex', alignItems: 'center', justifyContent: 'center',
    boxShadow: `0 12px 32px ${colour}40`, transition: 'transform 0.1s',
  };
}

function primaryBtn(): React.CSSProperties {
  return {
    width: '100%', padding: '12px 16px', background: theme.colors.primary, color: '#fff',
    border: 'none', borderRadius: theme.radius.md, fontSize: 14, fontWeight: 600,
    cursor: 'pointer', display: 'flex', alignItems: 'center', justifyContent: 'center', gap: 8,
  };
}

function getTimeOfDay(): string {
  const h = new Date().getHours();
  if (h < 6) return 'night';
  if (h < 12) return 'morning';
  if (h < 17) return 'afternoon';
  if (h < 21) return 'evening';
  return 'night';
}
Key changes that remove all 22 errors

Added DetectionResult interface at the top вАФ defines exactly what result contains, so TypeScript stops treating it as unknown
Cast the API response: const data = (await api.detect(fd)) as DetectionResult вАФ tells TypeScript the shape
Replaced any types: (err as Error) instead of any, properly typed sort callbacks
Pre-sorted the probabilities into a typed array вАФ [string, number][] вАФ before the .map, avoiding the inline sort that was causing any errors
if statements instead of && operator for the cleanup вАФ clearer and TypeScript-friendlier

typescriptimport { useState, useRef, useEffect } from 'react';
import { Mic, MicOff, Loader2, CheckCircle, AlertCircle, Thermometer } from 'lucide-react';
import { theme } from '../lib/theme';
import { api } from '../lib/api';
import { CLASS_LABEL, CLASS_EMOJI, CLASS_COLOUR } from '../components/shared';
import { TopBar } from '../components/TopBar';

const RECORDING_DURATION_MS = 4000;
type Stage = 'idle' | 'requesting' | 'recording' | 'processing' | 'result' | 'error';

interface DetectionResult {
  id: string;
  primaryCause: string;
  primaryConfidence: number;
  contextAdjustedCause: string;
  fusionApplied: boolean;
  fusionReason?: string;
  recommendation: string;
  actionItems: string[];
  allProbabilities: Record<string, number>;
  modelLatencyMs: number;
  totalLatencyMs: number;
  timestamp: string;
}

export function DetectScreen({ onDetected }: { onDetected: () => void }) {
  const [stage, setStage] = useState<Stage>('idle');
  const [error, setError] = useState<string | null>(null);
  const [result, setResult] = useState<DetectionResult | null>(null);
  const [progress, setProgress] = useState(0);
  const [temp, setTemp] = useState<number | null>(null);

  const recorderRef = useRef<MediaRecorder | null>(null);
  const chunksRef = useRef<Blob[]>([]);
  const streamRef = useRef<MediaStream | null>(null);
  const timerRef = useRef<number | null>(null);
  const progRef = useRef<number | null>(null);

  useEffect(() => () => {
    if (timerRef.current) clearTimeout(timerRef.current);
    if (progRef.current) clearInterval(progRef.current);
    streamRef.current?.getTracks().forEach((t) => t.stop());
  }, []);

  const start = async () => {
    setError(null);
    setResult(null);
    setStage('requesting');
    try {
      const stream = await navigator.mediaDevices.getUserMedia({
        audio: { channelCount: 1, sampleRate: 22050 },
      });
      streamRef.current = stream;
      const mimeType = MediaRecorder.isTypeSupported('audio/webm;codecs=opus')
        ? 'audio/webm;codecs=opus'
        : 'audio/webm';
      const recorder = new MediaRecorder(stream, { mimeType });
      recorderRef.current = recorder;
      chunksRef.current = [];
      recorder.ondataavailable = (e) => {
        if (e.data.size > 0) chunksRef.current.push(e.data);
      };
      recorder.onstop = handleStop;
      recorder.start();
      setStage('recording');
      const startTime = Date.now();
      progRef.current = window.setInterval(() => {
        setProgress(Math.min(100, ((Date.now() - startTime) / RECORDING_DURATION_MS) * 100));
      }, 50);
      timerRef.current = window.setTimeout(stop, RECORDING_DURATION_MS);
    } catch (err) {
      setStage('error');
      const e = err as Error;
      setError(
        e.name === 'NotAllowedError'
          ? 'Microphone permission denied. Please enable it in your browser settings.'
          : 'Could not access microphone.',
      );
    }
  };

  const stop = () => {
    if (timerRef.current) clearTimeout(timerRef.current);
    if (progRef.current) clearInterval(progRef.current);
    if (recorderRef.current?.state === 'recording') recorderRef.current.stop();
    streamRef.current?.getTracks().forEach((t) => t.stop());
  };

  const handleStop = async () => {
    setStage('processing');
    const blob = new Blob(chunksRef.current, { type: 'audio/webm' });
    if (blob.size < 2000) {
      setStage('error');
      setError('Recording too short. Please try again.');
      return;
    }
    try {
      const fd = new FormData();
      fd.append('audio', blob, 'cry.webm');
      fd.append('timeOfDay', getTimeOfDay());
      const data = (await api.detect(fd)) as DetectionResult;
      setResult(data);
      onDetected();
      setStage('result');
    } catch (err) {
      setStage('error');
      setError((err as Error).message || 'Could not process the recording.');
    }
  };

  const reset = () => {
    setStage('idle');
    setResult(null);
    setError(null);
    setProgress(0);
  };

  const adjustTemp = async (delta: number) => {
    const newVal = parseFloat(((temp ?? 22) + delta).toFixed(1));
    setTemp(newVal);
    try {
      await api.reportTemperature(newVal);
      onDetected();
    } catch {
      // silent вАФ UI already updated
    }
  };

  return (
    <div style={{ paddingBottom: 90 }}>
      <TopBar title="CrySense" subtitle="Tap to detect what your baby needs" />

      <div style={{ padding: '28px 20px', display: 'flex', flexDirection: 'column', alignItems: 'center' }}>

        <div style={{
          width: '100%', maxWidth: 420, background: theme.colors.surface,
          border: `1px solid ${theme.colors.border}`, borderRadius: theme.radius.lg,
          padding: 16, marginBottom: 28, display: 'flex', alignItems: 'center', gap: 12,
        }}>
          <div style={{
            width: 40, height: 40, background: `${theme.colors.info}15`,
            color: theme.colors.info, borderRadius: 999,
            display: 'flex', alignItems: 'center', justifyContent: 'center',
          }}>
            <Thermometer size={18} />
          </div>
          <div style={{ flex: 1, minWidth: 0 }}>
            <div style={{
              fontSize: 11, color: theme.colors.textMuted, fontWeight: 600,
              letterSpacing: '0.05em', textTransform: 'uppercase',
            }}>
              Room Temperature
            </div>
            <div style={{ fontSize: 18, fontWeight: 700, color: theme.colors.text, marginTop: 1 }}>
              {temp !== null ? `${temp.toFixed(1)}¬∞C` : 'вАФ'}
            </div>
          </div>
          <div style={{ display: 'flex', gap: 4 }}>
            {[-0.5, 0.5].map((d) => (
              <button
                key={d}
                onClick={() => adjustTemp(d)}
                style={{
                  width: 32, height: 32, borderRadius: theme.radius.md,
                  background: theme.colors.surfaceAlt,
                  border: `1px solid ${theme.colors.border}`,
                  cursor: 'pointer', fontWeight: 700, color: theme.colors.text,
                }}
              >
                {d > 0 ? '+' : 'вИТ'}
              </button>
            ))}
          </div>
        </div>

        {stage === 'idle' && (
          <button onClick={start} style={tapStyle(theme.colors.primary)}>
            <Mic size={56} color="#fff" />
          </button>
        )}
        {stage === 'requesting' && (
          <div style={tapStyle(theme.colors.textMuted)}>
            <Loader2 size={48} color="#fff" className="spin" />
          </div>
        )}
        {stage === 'recording' && (
          <div style={{ position: 'relative' }}>
            <svg width={200} height={200} style={{ position: 'absolute', transform: 'rotate(-90deg)' }}>
              <circle cx={100} cy={100} r={92} fill="none"
                stroke={`${theme.colors.primary}20`} strokeWidth={5} />
              <circle cx={100} cy={100} r={92} fill="none"
                stroke={theme.colors.primary} strokeWidth={5} strokeLinecap="round"
                strokeDasharray={`${(progress / 100) * 578} 578`}
                style={{ transition: 'stroke-dasharray 0.05s linear' }} />
            </svg>
            <button onClick={stop} style={tapStyle(theme.colors.danger)}>
              <MicOff size={56} color="#fff" />
            </button>
          </div>
        )}
        {stage === 'processing' && (
          <div style={tapStyle(theme.colors.primary)}>
            <Loader2 size={48} color="#fff" className="spin" />
          </div>
        )}

        {(stage === 'idle' || stage === 'recording' || stage === 'processing') && (
          <p style={{ marginTop: 24, fontSize: 14, color: theme.colors.textMuted, textAlign: 'center' }}>
            {stage === 'idle' && 'Tap when baby is crying'}
            {stage === 'recording' && `ListeningвА¶ ${Math.round(progress)}%`}
            {stage === 'processing' && 'Analysing the cryвА¶'}
          </p>
        )}

        {stage === 'result' && result && <ResultCard result={result} onReset={reset} />}

        {stage === 'error' && (
          <div style={{
            width: '100%', maxWidth: 420, background: `${theme.colors.danger}08`,
            border: `1px solid ${theme.colors.danger}30`, borderRadius: theme.radius.lg,
            padding: 20, textAlign: 'center', marginTop: 24,
          }}>
            <AlertCircle size={28} color={theme.colors.danger} style={{ marginBottom: 8 }} />
            <p style={{ color: theme.colors.danger, marginBottom: 16, fontSize: 14 }}>{error}</p>
            <button onClick={reset} style={primaryBtn()}>Try again</button>
          </div>
        )}
      </div>
    </div>
  );
}

function ResultCard({ result, onReset }: { result: DetectionResult; onReset: () => void }) {
  const cause = result.contextAdjustedCause;
  const colour = CLASS_COLOUR[cause];
  const confPct = Math.round(result.primaryConfidence * 100);

  const sortedProbs: [string, number][] = Object.entries(result.allProbabilities)
    .sort((a, b) => b[1] - a[1]);

  return (

    }}>

            </div>
          ))}
        </div>

        <div style={{ marginTop: 20, paddingTop: 16, borderTop: `1px solid ${theme.colors.borderLight}` }}>
          {sortedProbs.map(([cls, prob]) => (
            <div key={cls} style={{ marginBottom: 8 }}>
              <div style={{ display: 'flex', justifyContent: 'space-between', fontSize: 12, marginBottom: 4 }}>

                <span style={{ color: theme.colors.textMuted }}>{Math.round(prob * 100)}%</span>
              </div>
              <div style={{ height: 4, background: theme.colors.surfaceAlt, borderRadius: 2 }}>
                <div style={{
                  height: '100%', width: `${prob * 100}%`,
                  background: CLASS_COLOUR[cls], borderRadius: 2, transition: 'width 0.4s',
                }} />
              </div>
            </div>
          ))}
        </div>

        {result.fusionApplied && result.fusionReason && (
          <div style={{
            marginTop: 16, padding: 12, background: `${theme.colors.warning}10`,
            border: `1px solid ${theme.colors.warning}30`, borderRadius: theme.radius.md,
            fontSize: 12, lineHeight: 1.5, color: theme.colors.text,
          }}>
            <strong style={{ color: theme.colors.warning }}>Context note: </strong>
            {result.fusionReason}
          </div>
        )}

        <button onClick={onReset} style={{ ...primaryBtn(), marginTop: 20 }}>
          <Mic size={16} /> Detect another cry
        </button>
      </div>
    </div>
  );
}

function tapStyle(colour: string): React.CSSProperties {
  return {
    width: 200, height: 200, borderRadius: '50%', background: colour, border: 'none',
    cursor: 'pointer', display: 'flex', alignItems: 'center', justifyContent: 'center',
    boxShadow: `0 12px 32px ${colour}40`, transition: 'transform 0.1s',
  };
}

function primaryBtn(): React.CSSProperties {
  return {
    width: '100%', padding: '12px 16px', background: theme.colors.primary, color: '#fff',
    border: 'none', borderRadius: theme.radius.md, fontSize: 14, fontWeight: 600,
    cursor: 'pointer', display: 'flex', alignItems: 'center', justifyContent: 'center', gap: 8,
  };
}

function getTimeOfDay(): string {
  const h = new Date().getHours();
  if (h < 6) return 'night';
  if (h < 12) return 'morning';
  if (h < 17) return 'afternoon';
  if (h < 21) return 'evening';
  return 'night';
}

Right now it's stark white which feels clinical. I'll change it to a soft cream/peach background with the coral accent staying.
Open src/lib/theme.ts, select all, and replace with this:
typescriptexport const theme = {
  colors: {
    // Coral accent (kept)
    primary: '#FF6B5B',
    primaryDark: '#E84F3F',
    primaryLight: '#FFE8E5',

    // Warm neutral palette вАФ cream & soft peach undertones
    background: '#FFF8F3',      // soft cream
    surface: '#FFFFFF',          // pure white for cards
    surfaceAlt: '#FDF1E8',       // peach-tinted alt surface
    surfaceWarm: '#FFEDE3',      // warmer accent surface
    border: '#F0E0D2',           // soft tan border
    borderLight: '#F8EBDE',      // even softer border

    // Text вАФ warm dark instead of pure black
    text: '#2D1810',             // warm dark brown
    textMuted: '#8B6F5C',        // muted brown
    textLight: '#B89B85',        // light tan

    // Semantic
    success: '#10B981',
    warning: '#F59E0B',
    danger: '#EF4444',
    info: '#3B82F6',

    // Cry classes
    hunger: '#F59E0B',
    pain: '#EF4444',
    discomfort: '#8B5CF6',
    sleepiness: '#3B82F6',
  },
  spacing: { xs: 4, sm: 8, md: 16, lg: 24, xl: 32, xxl: 48 },
  radius: { sm: 6, md: 10, lg: 16, xl: 24, full: 999 },
  fonts: {
    display: "'Inter', system-ui, -apple-system, sans-serif",
    body: "'Inter', system-ui, -apple-system, sans-serif",
  },
};
Save the file. Your dev server should hot-reload and you'll see the change immediately вАФ soft cream background, warm peach surfaces, brown text instead of black, and the coral mic button now pops more against the warmer base.

Here's the realistic path for your final year project вАФ the goal is to demo it to your supervisor from a public URL.
The deployment strategy
You have three services to deploy, each with different needs:
ServiceSizeFree hosting that worksFastAPI model serviceHeavy (ONNX + librosa + ffmpeg)Render (free tier) or Fly.ioNestJS backendSmallRender, Railway, or Fly.ioReact frontendTiny (static files)Vercel or Netlify (best free tiers)
I recommend Render for both backends and Vercel for the frontend. All free, all support GitHub auto-deploy. Let's go.

Step 1: Push everything to GitHub
If you haven't already:
powershellcd C:\Users\somto\Desktop\finalyear\crysensecode
git init
git add .
git commit -m "Initial CrySense project"
Create three separate .gitignore checks вАФ your crysense.db, node_modules/, __pycache__/, .env, and venv/ should NOT be in git. Verify with:
powershellgit status
If .env or models/ files show up, add them to .gitignore first. Your model .onnx file IS okay to commit (we need it deployed), but .env and database files must stay local.
Then create a new GitHub repo at github.com/new and push:
powershellgit remote add origin https://github.com/YOUR_USERNAME/crysense.git
git branch -M main
git push -u origin main

Step 2: Prepare the FastAPI service for production
Make sure model-api/requirements.txt is complete:
fastapi==0.115.0
uvicorn[standard]==0.30.6
python-multipart==0.0.9
onnxruntime==1.18.0
librosa==0.10.2
noisereduce==3.0.2
numpy==1.26.4
soundfile==0.12.1
pydantic==2.9.2
imageio-ffmpeg==0.5.1
